  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d5c69fc6-9eef-4554-b887-d4c9ae50db19'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer12461406960453065739">Ever since Jacob Reckless was a child, he has been escaping to a hidden world through a portal in his father's abandoned study. Over the years, he has made a name for himself as a finder of enchanted items and buried secrets.   <span id="freeText12461406960453065739" style="display:none">Ever since Jacob Reckless was a child, he has been escaping to a hidden world through a portal in his father's abandoned study. Over the years, he has made a name for himself as a finder of enchanted items and buried secrets. He's also made many enemies and allies--most important, Fox, a beautiful shape-shifting vixen whom Jacob cares for more than he lets on.<br /><br />But life in this other world is about to change. Tragedy strikes when Jacob's younger brother, Will, follows him through the portal. Brutally attacked, Will is infected with a curse that is quickly transforming him into a Goyl--a ruthless killing machine, with skin made of stone.<br /><br />Jacob is prepared to fight to save his brother, but in a land built on trickery and lies, Jacob will need all the wit, courage, and reckless spirit he can summon to reverse the dark spell--before it's too late.</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_8600762').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_8600762').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_8600762').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

</script></div>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Book 1 was originally just called "Reckless" but it was renamed and republished as "Reckless: The Petrified Flesh."<br/>Similarly, book 2 was first release<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Book 1 was originally just called "Reckless" but it was renamed and republished as "Reckless: The Petrified Flesh."<br />Similarly, book 2 was first released as "Fearless" but it has since been re-released as "Reckless 2: Living Shadows."<br />Book 3 was originally called "Heartless," but it's published title is "Reckless 3: The Golden Yarn."<br />Book 4 will be "The Islands of the Fox" (not yet released), and book 5's title has not be announced yet.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8081422898557890297"><a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=KPelCuFSOMY' rel='nofollow noopener'>Click here</a> to watch a video review of this book on my channel, <i>From Beginning to Bookend</i>.<br/><br/>When Jacob Reckless was a boy, he discovered another world on the other side of the mirror in his father’s abandoned study. After keeping the mirror world secret for twelve years, Jacob’s younger brother finds his way through the mirror and is terminally cursed. Now Jacob and his brother must journey to the most dangerous territories of the mirror world to bargain with untrustworthy creatures to reverse the </span>
  <span id="freeText8081422898557890297" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=KPelCuFSOMY" rel="nofollow noopener">Click here</a> to watch a video review of this book on my channel, <i>From Beginning to Bookend</i>.<br /><br />When Jacob Reckless was a boy, he discovered another world on the other side of the mirror in his father’s abandoned study. After keeping the mirror world secret for twelve years, Jacob’s younger brother finds his way through the mirror and is terminally cursed. Now Jacob and his brother must journey to the most dangerous territories of the mirror world to bargain with untrustworthy creatures to reverse the curse before it’s too late. <br /><br /><i>There was no place [Jacob] called home, either in this world or the other. He always yearned for unknown places, secrets revealed, treasure found . . . there was so much he still hadn’t seen.</i> <br /><br /><i>The Petrified Flesh</i> makes a departure from the average young adult novel. Instead of frou frou love triangles or a teen girl defying the odds, this book features a young man motivated by grief and a grim world based on the darker aspects of fairy tales, myth and lore. Because of its violent content (children being shot) and creepy characters (a murderer wearing a suit made of human flesh), this book is recommended for a mature audience. <br /><br /><i>How the Dark Fairy would have enjoyed killing her. A poisoned comb, a dress that would eat into her flesh when she put it on in front of her golden mirrors. How she would scream and scratch her skin, so much softer than that of her bridegroom.</i> <br /><br />The mirror world, fraught with war and brimming with dangerous beings, is nonetheless a magical place filled with “<i>crystal caves, black lakes, and petrified forests</i>.” With mythical creatures, bustling cities, and unique world rules, Funke offers readers a fully realized fantasy world. <br /><br /><i>Dwarf trading posts could be found in every corner of this world, despite the fact that they were nearly half the size of their human customers.</i> <br /><br /><i>Many cities behind the mirror hired Giantlings, men who claimed their direct descent from the extinct Giants, as guards. [. . .] Giantlings were also vastly popular as mercenaries, despite their reputation for being rather dimwitted.</i> <br /><br /><i>The cave’s ground was covered with bones, as all Ogres loved to surround themselves with their leftovers. Some even built music instruments or sculptures from their victims’ remains; others recited poetry while they cooked them.</i> <br /><br />Before the story concludes, unicorns will be spotted, adventures will be had, and tragedy will strike.<br /> <br /><i>The Petrified Flesh</i> is a morbid delight.</span>

<div id="review_109552023" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/109552023" />
    <a title="★ Jess " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2683062-jess"><img alt="★ Jess " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466182835p2/2683062.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/109552023?book_show_action=true">Jul 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="★ Jess " class="user" itemprop="url" name="★ Jess " href="/user/show/2683062-jess">★ Jess </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781905294855" href="/book/show/8600762-reckless">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2683062-jess?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2683062-jess?shelf=2-stars-average">2-stars-average</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2683062-jess?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer109552023" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13255127503995794397">Oh dear....<br/>What a disappointing book. The very pages stunk of mediocrity. <br/>The main issue with 'Reckless' lies solely with the characters: Cornelia Funke plunges us right into the middle of the story, with no detail on the characters what-so-ever. Jacob, Will and Clara are possibly THE WORST leads in a novel I have ever read about. There is absolutely no chemistry between them. I couldn't care less about what happens to them. <br/>I imagine Cornelia Funke's brainstorming of these characters was <s>a litt</s></span>
  <span id="freeText13255127503995794397" style="display:none">Oh dear....<br />What a disappointing book. The very pages stunk of mediocrity. <br />The main issue with 'Reckless' lies solely with the characters: Cornelia Funke plunges us right into the middle of the story, with no detail on the characters what-so-ever. Jacob, Will and Clara are possibly THE WORST leads in a novel I have ever read about. There is absolutely no chemistry between them. I couldn't care less about what happens to them. <br />I imagine Cornelia Funke's brainstorming of these characters was <s>a little</s> a lot like this: <br /><br /><i><b>Cornelia:</b>K, so, Jacob is the main character, Will is his brother and Clara is Will's girlfriend. Getitgotitgood, now onto the story... <br /><b>Editor:</b> No, wait a second Corny, you need a bit more detail. <br /><b>Cornelia:</b>: Really? Okay, ummm...Will and Clara met in a hospital and totally fell in love. <br /><b>Editor:</b>FREAKIN' PERFECT!</i> <br /><br />Im not even kidding, that is all the information we got on these characters. Will and Clara, the couple who is 'head over heels desperately in love', never show any affection for each other. Ever. <br />The plot of 'Reckless' is basically this: Will gets turned into a Goyl (a species of monsters made out of stone who are evil for the hell of it) , and Jacob and Clara have to save him. <br />The problem (one of trillions) is this: Will gets no page-time before the transformation. His first scene is him turning into the Goyl. This means that the reader doesn't care for him, and I couldn't give a rats ass weather he is saved or not. <br />Oh, and for the majority of the 345 pages, everybody treats Will like his is a baby. Just because he is the younger sibling, doesn't mean he needs to be treated like a two year old, when he is, in fact, graduated from high school. <br />The characters are so annoying and less one-dimensional (or more, I guess...) then even <a href="http://www.shockya.com/news/wp-content/uploads/new_moon_bella_teaser_poster.jpg " rel="nofollow noopener">this person</a><br /><br />Also. the un-named world-behind-the-mirror seems like a cheap, much less thought through version of The Inkworld in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28195.Inkspell__Inkheart___2_" title="Inkspell (Inkheart, #2) by Cornelia Funke" rel="nofollow noopener">Inkspell</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2325825.Inkdeath__Inkheart___3_" title="Inkdeath (Inkheart, #3) by Cornelia Funke" rel="nofollow noopener">Inkdeath</a> also by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15873.Cornelia_Funke" title="Cornelia Funke" rel="nofollow noopener">Cornelia Funke</a>. <br /><br />Normally, I love Cornelia Funke-she is in my list of favorite authors, along side <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3389.Stephen_King" title="Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">Stephen King</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1077326.J_K__Rowling" title="J.K. Rowling" rel="nofollow noopener">J.K. Rowling</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4273.Roald_Dahl" title="Roald Dahl" rel="nofollow noopener">Roald Dahl</a>. The 'Inkheart trilogy' are some of my favorite books, and The Thief Lord is sensational. <br />Maybe I just had super high expectations for her new book. I had, after all, been following Funke's blog updates since she announced the idea for 'Reckless', eagerly counting down the days to its release. <br />None the less, this was really not enjoyable. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13255127503995794397" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/32494578-the-petrified-flesh">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=retelling">retelling</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1643010365" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8073931296121157161"><b>I had no idea what to expect from this but I reeeeally liked it.</b> I know I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28194.Inkheart__Inkworld___1_' title='Inkheart (Inkworld, #1) by Cornelia Funke' rel='nofollow noopener'>Inkheart</a> 52 million years ago. But I didn't like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/100464.Dragon_Rider__Dragon_Rider___1_' title='Dragon Rider (Dragon Rider, #1) by Cornelia Funke' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dragon Rider</a> much at all, so it didn't really occur to me I'd want to read more Cornelia Funke. I'M SO GLAD I DID. <b>This was stuffed with dark vicious stabby fairy tale fantasticness.</b> My kind of story basically.<br/><br/>(NOTE: apparently this is actually an edition that's been editing again and rewritten a bit by Cornelia Funke before republishing with this cover?? So I can't com</span>
  <span id="freeText8073931296121157161" style="display:none"><b>I had no idea what to expect from this but I reeeeally liked it.</b> I know I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28194.Inkheart__Inkworld___1_" title="Inkheart (Inkworld, #1) by Cornelia Funke" rel="nofollow noopener">Inkheart</a> 52 million years ago. But I didn't like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/100464.Dragon_Rider__Dragon_Rider___1_" title="Dragon Rider (Dragon Rider, #1) by Cornelia Funke" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragon Rider</a> much at all, so it didn't really occur to me I'd want to read more Cornelia Funke. I'M SO GLAD I DID. <b>This was stuffed with dark vicious stabby fairy tale fantasticness.</b> My kind of story basically.<br /><br />(NOTE: apparently this is actually an edition that's been editing again and rewritten a bit by Cornelia Funke before republishing with this cover?? So I can't compare it to the original, of course, but anyway. LOVE THE COVER SO BAD.)<br /><br /><b>The best part of this book is obviously the Mirrorworld.</b> I had in the back of my mind it was going to be a chill sort of whimsy middle-grade thing? BUT HAHAH NO CAIT. It's very dark. There's torture and dark woods and creepy monsters and warped romances and people getting shot and cut and stabbed and aaall the things. <b>It doesn't graphically describe anything, though?</b> So I suppose small poptart readers won't die reading this.<br /><br /><b>It's stuffed with fairy tale references too.</b> #winningatlife I <i>adore</i> fairy tales and this takes them from a dark angle. I particularly like how it had a Sleeping Beauty vibe going on but this time it was the BOY who would need the GIRL to wake him with a kiss. I love that!!! And the style was also very fairy-tale-like, with just the right amount of description.<br /><br /><b>I also adored how it's a brother story.</b> I like brother stories. Like the easies way to get me snabbled into a book is to say either (A) there's food in here, or (B) there are siblings bonding in here. SO THIS WINS FOR B!! Fails a bit for A. They literally never eat. But I suppose the strength of magical quests can fill your stomach? (FYI I would die. I need my snacks.) <b>So Jacob Reckless is like a treasure hunter in the mirrorworld because he hates his world.</b> I don't know why. But who wouldn't? Reality is dumb. Then his little bro, Will, follows him in and (1) gets attacked or something and starts to turn into a jade-skinned-monster, (2) which means Jacob has to move hell AND high water to fix him, (3) which then turns out into quest after bloody quest and everyone nearly (or does) die and the vicious fairies try to kill everyone and go to war and Jacob gets nearly mauled by unicorns AGAIN and it's just tragedy and heartbreak -- AND I LOVE IT.<br /><br /><b>I'm a <i>little</i> bit ticked off at the "romance" though.</b> Like Jacob definitely sleeps around (this is firmly eluded to) but he's definitely in love with a shape-shifter fox. She loves him back. Do they talk about it? NO. NEVER. It's very frustrating, because she'll hate him when he kisses someone else but yet she won't confess her feelings???? I loved Fox but at the same time she was only there for sexual tension and that annoyed me. <b>Basically the female characters in this book were seriously lacking in active and interesting rolls.</b><br /><br /><b>And honestly? I do have a BIGGER quibble too: I felt the book was pretty emotionless.</b> Just the writing style. I never knew what Jacob felt for most of the book. Or what anyone else felt. DARN YOU WHERE ARE MY FEELINGS. I was obsessed by the world and all the dark magic but at the same time...I was <b>very emotionally detached</b>. I wanted to <i>care</i> but it was a bit of a struggle. I don't know if this is a translation thing???? Or me being a Vulcan???? But it was a big problem for me.<br /><br /><b>ALL IN ALL: this is a darkly vicious fairy tale of monsters and murder, and I really adored it!</b> It's left me feeling rather inspired and excited. Which is exactly the kind of feel I want to finish a book with! I adored Jacob and his stony stubbornness to save his brother from turning into stone. I wish he'd, like, had feelings, but WHATEVER. CAN'T HAVE EVERYTHING. And the world is just A+ for creepy wonder.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8073931296121157161" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_123632467" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/123632467" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/123632467?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9783791504858" href="/book/show/7894237-steinernes-fleisch">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer123632467" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6806838351447426838">Some people call Cornelia Funke the German J.K. Rowling. She apparently hates to be called so (I like that about her). Of course she would, after all, she is her very own person with her very unique style. The only connection: they both write (or at least started with) children's books.<br/><br/>I always read books in their original language if I can, but although German is my mother tongue, I usually don't find German authors appealing (classics aside). <br/>With Cornelia Funke it's totally different. Her wri</span>
  <span id="freeText6806838351447426838" style="display:none">Some people call Cornelia Funke the German J.K. Rowling. She apparently hates to be called so (I like that about her). Of course she would, after all, she is her very own person with her very unique style. The only connection: they both write (or at least started with) children's books.<br><br>I always read books in their original language if I can, but although German is my mother tongue, I usually don't find German authors appealing (classics aside). <br>With Cornelia Funke it's totally different. Her writing style is enthralling and reminds me that my language can be magical and beautiful too and has a lot of history.<br><br>The first book I've read of this author was the famous <b>Inkheart</b> that made her an instant international success. I wanted to be a silvertongue sooo badly and never ever wanted to leave the world of Littlefinger.<br><br>So imagine my surprise when I started this new trilogy, called <b>Reckless</b> (that's the main title for all three books in German with subtitles like <i>Steinernes Fleisch</i>, meaning flesh of stone) and LOVED IT SO MUCH <u>MORE</u>!<br><br>Words don't do my feelings justice - which is funny considering that a story consists of nothing else.<br>Cornelia Funke is like a siren singing her song, drawing you in - just with a happier ending. And it's not just her impeccable way of showing the beauty of the German language but also her very own illustrations that are a feast for the eyes! Oh, yes, in case you didn't know: she started out as an illustrator, then wrote her first book and has been illustrating her own books ever since!<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449248975i/17256349._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This story is about the brothers Jacob and Will Reckless whose names were inspired by the brothers Grimm (they were called Willhelm and Jakob). They had a very rough start in life because their father simply disappeared, which <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[broke their mother, leading to her death even and <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> set the tone for their later life. <br><br>I can't help but have a heavy heart about the background story of Jacob and Will regarding the disappearance of their father because of the author's own history. It wasn't her father who left. It was more tragic than that. After being an international success, she and her husband decided to move to Los Angeles with their two children - to a beautiful house with a gigantic garden (I think I even saw a fairy in one of the photographs). Two months later, her husband died of cancer (they had no idea he had it). It was a blow from which she only recovered slowly (there were some updates now and then from her sister who runs her blog) and whenever I read about Mo or Jacob (the two trilogies being somewhat darker than her other books, deeper in meaning in my opinion), there is this slight tug ... this darkness I can feel. But not in a bad way. As Cornelia Funke (and J.K. Rowling, incidentally) often try to explain to "concerned parents": dark stories need to be told as well and especially children can handle more than adults give them credit for. Besides, they need to learn that there is darkness in the world and why not letting them learn from books while they are in a comforting and secure environment?! What is more, stories like this also teach the reader how to HANDLE darkness!<br><br>Anyway, back to the story ...<br>While Jacob does everything to earn his family name (without being stupid), his younger brother is more gentle. <br>One night, right at the beginning of this story, when Jacob is only 12, he discovers a magical land behind a mirror in his father's study that is inhabited by all the creatures we know from fairy tales (NOT the fluffy Disney versions)!<br>Thus begin his adventures there that lead him away from his family more and more often. <br>However, one day (12 years later) Will discovers his secret, follows him ... and yeah, it doesn't go so well - leading to an epic quest.<br><br>What I loved was how different the brothers were and that Jacob, despite not wanting to be close to someone (for fear of getting hurt), would do ANYTHING for his brother.<br>An often quoted description of this first book was <i>Es war einmal ein Junge, der auszog, das Fürchten zu lernen</i> which is the title of the Grimm fairy tale "The Story of the Youth Who Went Forth to Learn What Fear Was" (see what she did there?).<br>The author has a wonderful way of taking something that is already there, has roots and tradition, and artfully rearranging it to make a new story from it.<br><br>Since I've always loved fairy tales (the fluffy ones as well as the darker, original versions), I ADORED the Mirrorworld with the tailor, dwarves, fairies, witches, goyls, ... and all the magical items. What I wouldn't give to be able to walk through it (no matter how dangerous) ... but wait, I just did! ;)<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449248975i/17256350.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Cornelia Funke really makes the world come to life, dark and bright sides alike, and you can almost taste the sweets of the ginger bread house, smell the roses in the eternally sleeping castle (or prick your finger if you're not careful), hear leaves rustle in the wind, ...<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449248975i/17256351.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449248975i/17256352.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>("The Dark Sister" for those of you, who were wondering.)<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449248975i/17256353.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>... which is why I will return to Mirrorworld right away, in the next book!<br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="6806838351447426838" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_112997795" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/112997795" />
    <a title="Reading Teen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3329955-reading-teen"><img alt="Reading Teen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294347905p2/3329955.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/112997795?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reading Teen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reading Teen" href="/user/show/3329955-reading-teen">Reading Teen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer112997795" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10893109724444298988">I picked this book up at ALA 10 for my ten-year-old daughter. I got it signed for her and everything. She loved the Inkheart series and was really excited to start reading it, but after about 15 pages, she brought it to me and said, "I don't understand what's happening, this book makes no sense." So, I told her that I'd read it, and try to explain it to her. I am SO glad that I started this book....for two reasons. First, my ten-year-old is not ready for it. There was way too much bone-chilling </span>
  <span id="freeText10893109724444298988" style="display:none">I picked this book up at ALA 10 for my ten-year-old daughter. I got it signed for her and everything. She loved the Inkheart series and was really excited to start reading it, but after about 15 pages, she brought it to me and said, "I don't understand what's happening, this book makes no sense." So, I told her that I'd read it, and try to explain it to her. I am SO glad that I started this book....for two reasons. First, my ten-year-old is not ready for it. There was way too much bone-chilling creepiness, and there was also quite a lot of adult innuendo (the main character is 24) that she either wouldn't understand, or shouldn't be reading at ten.<br /><br />The second reason is that I REALLY liked it a lot!! Unfortunately, if she hadn't brought it to me, I don't know that I would have ever picked it up, which makes me sad because I'm afraid that people who would love it, won't read it because it's marked (presently anyway) for 9-12 year olds. <br /><br />So, why did I like this book so much? It was like The Lord of the Rings crossed with The Brothers Grimm Fairy Tales. I loved reading about the world behind the mirror! There were witches, and fairies, and dwarfs, and creepy stone creatures called Goyl. Then there were familiar fairy tale characters like Snow White and Sleeping Beauty (who was still sleeping because her prince never came for her). The story changes perspective several times as it is told by many different points of view, including Jacob, a loner who finds his place in this alternate world, Jacob's loyal female companion and shape-shifter, Fox, Jacob's brother, Will, who is rapidly turning into a Goyl, Will's fiery girlfriend, Clara, Hentzau, the captain of the evil Goyl King's army, and a few others. Though I think it might be confusing for younger readers, I thoroughly enjoyed reading from all these points of view. It was even interesting reading from the villain's outlook! <br /><br />The creepy-factor was big in this book, too. If you're a fan of the Brothers Grimm or Tim Burton type movies, you will definitely appreciate the bizarre, and eerily terrifying creatures in Reckless. Some of them seriously gave me chills. "The Tailor"....that's all I'm saying. <br /><br />I loved everything about this mystical world that Cornelia Funke twisted to make her own. I never knew what was going to happen next, or what creature they would encounter on their quest to free Will from the flesh-eating stone that was consuming him. The only complaint that I have is that I wish that we were able to get to know the characters a little better. I didn't feel like I got to know Jacob, or Will very well, which made it hard for me to care as much about what happened to them. Hopefully they will be fleshed out a little more in the next book which I can't wait to read! I hope that you won't let the age recommendation keep you from this book, and I hope you'll love it as much as I did.<br /><br />Reckless is an Epic adventure with a creepy twist on all the Fairytales we know and love. "If you're looking for happily ever after, you've come to the wrong place."<br /><br />~Andye (<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://ReadingTeen.net/">http://ReadingTeen.net/</a>)</span>
  <a data-text-id="10893109724444298988" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_270851214" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/270851214" />
    <a title="Lydia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7589403-lydia"><img alt="Lydia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328109460p2/7589403.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/270851214?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lydia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lydia" href="/user/show/7589403-lydia">Lydia</a>
      </span>

        rated it

<span id="freeTextContainer17935120823928767012">I am extremely happy to write a review of this book. It was simply excellent. If you can imagine the fantasy of Tolkien, with the emotional connectivity of modern stories, and an anti-hero Paul Newman would be proud of, you will get a little taste of this tale. <br/><br/>The modern idea of taking timeless fairy tales and "revealing" their true, much darker, origins is an idea Funke plays out in this novel where a young man named Jacob runs from the pain of his youth, through a looking glass, and chooses t</span>
  <span id="freeText17935120823928767012" style="display:none">I am extremely happy to write a review of this book. It was simply excellent. If you can imagine the fantasy of Tolkien, with the emotional connectivity of modern stories, and an anti-hero Paul Newman would be proud of, you will get a little taste of this tale. <br /><br />The modern idea of taking timeless fairy tales and "revealing" their true, much darker, origins is an idea Funke plays out in this novel where a young man named Jacob runs from the pain of his youth, through a looking glass, and chooses to face his fears in another, much more magical world. For yeas he dances back and forth between the two, becoming more drawn and entangled with the fantasy world than that of which he was born. <br /><br />Then, one day, his younger, gentler and vulnerable brother follows him through, and disaster strikes. Jacob, a now calamity-hardened treasure hunter, along with his vixen Fox (a woman who shape shifts), must risk everything to find a way to save his brother's life. This means dealing with an oft-deceitful dwarf, a conniving empress, blood thirsty unicorns, and the supremely powerful trickery of waring fairy sisters. <br /><br />Jacob's love is never spoken, and his devotion seems lacking. But it is his deeds and bravery that prove the bond of brotherhood. As true anti-heroes do, he creates a place in your heart when you know you should care for another. <br /><br />Funke who, according to a children's librarian I recently spoke to, is more widely read in Europe than J.K. Rowling, does a fantastical job weaving this magical story of courage in the face of adversity, and the bonds of love (yes, there is a girl in the mix) and brothers. </span>

<div id="review_700195582" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/700195582" />
    <a title="Arielle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6762949-arielle"><img alt="Arielle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452561487p2/6762949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/700195582?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arielle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arielle" href="/user/show/6762949-arielle">Arielle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6762949-arielle?shelf=in-translation">in-translation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6762949-arielle?shelf=fantasy-unusual">fantasy-unusual</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6762949-arielle?shelf=children">children</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6762949-arielle?shelf=faerytales">faerytales</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer700195582" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3682553700170095286">It's a little heartbreaking to give a Cornelia Funke book such a low rating. Though the Mirrorworld is certainly intriguing, the characters don't feel entirely fleshed out, and the plot rushes by at such a pace that it is all to easy to lose your bearing. The writing has none of the fluidity of the Inkworld series - it's almost difficult to believe the author is the same, though the themes and characters are similar - and Jacob is no Dustfinger. Such comparisons may seem unfair, but the fact rem</span>
  <span id="freeText3682553700170095286" style="display:none">It's a little heartbreaking to give a Cornelia Funke book such a low rating. Though the Mirrorworld is certainly intriguing, the characters don't feel entirely fleshed out, and the plot rushes by at such a pace that it is all to easy to lose your bearing. The writing has none of the fluidity of the Inkworld series - it's almost difficult to believe the author is the same, though the themes and characters are similar - and Jacob is no Dustfinger. Such comparisons may seem unfair, but the fact remains that the similarities to Inkheart are too great to ignore, and inevitably, when compared, Reckless falls short.<br /><br />Strangely enough, the book feels devoid of description - a little skeletal, no matter how crammed full of odd, stunningly unusual creatures it may be. It's a shame - there is so, so much potential, and Funke has proved herself more than capable with previous works. The stone-skinned Goyl, the wonderful shape-changing Fox, the dark Mirror world growing more and more like our own, the unusual (sometimes humourous) fairy-tale twists...<br /><br />I strongly believe this is largely down to the translation. Though I know Funke has a big role in choosing the english words that finally make it to the page, the fact remains that this translation lacks the grace of Anthea Bell's (translator of the Inkworld series, and of Dragon Rider) work.<br /><br />I will happily read the rest of the series in case the english settles into itself better otherwise I really will have to brush up on my German and try this in its native language.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3682553700170095286" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/981514-minli?shelf=mythic">mythic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/981514-minli?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer205557931" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15531031394972425919">I'm not sure if it's because this book was originally written in German, and German translated into English is clunky by default (have you ever had to read Weber? remember how fun that was?) but Cornelia Funke's style really takes some getting used to. It's not for everyone--I'm not even sure if it's for me. On one hand, the Mirrorworld was intriguing, and my favourite part was learning that the there were different types of Goyl based on the types of rocks. On the other, Jacob has got to be the</span>
  <span id="freeText15531031394972425919" style="display:none">I'm not sure if it's because this book was originally written in German, and German translated into English is clunky by default (have you ever had to read Weber? remember how fun that was?) but Cornelia Funke's style really takes some getting used to. It's not for everyone--I'm not even sure if it's for me. On one hand, the Mirrorworld was intriguing, and my favourite part was learning that the there were different types of Goyl based on the types of rocks. On the other, Jacob has got to be the most boring 24-year-old protagonist I've ever read. And I didn't get to spend enough time with Will to really understand what a tragedy it was to have lost him to the witch. It's a good thing I liked Clara and Fox.<br /><br />This book was originally classified as middle grade, and I cannot begin to tell you how wrong that is. There are some supremely disturbing scenes (allusions to sexual violence, torture, etc.) that make this book inappropriate for most tweens, at least not until they understand the nuances of those issues.<br /><br />Still, once I got into it, I kept turning the pages. Probably not something I'd re-read, but I might pick up the sequel to find out what happens.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15531031394972425919" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2001872831" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2001872831" />
    <a title="leynes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45198798-leynes"><img alt="leynes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593512704p2/45198798.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2001872831?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="leynes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="leynes" href="/user/show/45198798-leynes">leynes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9783791504858" href="/book/show/7894237-steinernes-fleisch">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2001872831" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11771624591796358199">It feels so good to be back! 2019 (so far) has been an amazing year for me in regards to rereading my all-time favourites. The last time I read <i>Reckless</i> by my literal queen Cornelia Funke (a local legend here in Germany, we all stan) was nearly 10 years ago. Ever since then, this series has held a special place in my heart. It has a similar vibe to Connie's <i>Ink</i> trilogy but instead of a fantasy world made of ink and words, in <i>Reckless</i>, we are introduced to a world made of glass and mirrors. <br/><br/>Jacob</span>
  <span id="freeText11771624591796358199" style="display:none">It feels so good to be back! 2019 (so far) has been an amazing year for me in regards to rereading my all-time favourites. The last time I read <i>Reckless</i> by my literal queen Cornelia Funke (a local legend here in Germany, we all stan) was nearly 10 years ago. Ever since then, this series has held a special place in my heart. It has a similar vibe to Connie's <i>Ink</i> trilogy but instead of a fantasy world made of ink and words, in <i>Reckless</i>, we are introduced to a world made of glass and mirrors. <br /><br />Jacob Reckless discovers one day that the mirror in his father's study is magical. Looking (or rather: not looking) at it in the right way transports you to a world in which fairy tales are true. Dwarves, elves, fairies, princesses and goyl – those are the creatures that inhabit this strange place called the Mirrorworld. Jacob soon chooses this world as his second, and then his first home. He flees from his unjoyous family in the real world, a father who abandoned them, a mother who never came to terms with that, and a younger brother who needs him more than anyone.<br /><br />In the Mirrorworld, Jacob made friends with Celeste, sometimes girl, sometimes fox. He underwent an apprenticeship with the renown treasure hunter Chanute, and soon follows in his footsteps. Over the course of ten years, Jacob has made a name for himself in the Mirrorworld. People pay him for his talent to get a hold of the rarest and most precious wonders, even the empress of Austry. <br /><br />The plot of <i>Reckless #1</i> follows Jacob, as he is faced with the difficult task of saving his brother, who for the first time in his life followed him through the Mirror, from turning into greenstone. Jacob never wanted his brother to discover his secret but due to his own carelessness, he now has to save his brothers life. To make matters worse, his brother's girlfriend Clara found a way into the Mirrorworld and refuses to leave Will behind. Together with Fox and the help of the dwarf Valiant, they embark on the mission to turn Will into a human again.<br /><br />On their adventure, they are faced with many creatures with whom readers of the Brother's Grimm will be familiar with. Cornelia Funke interwove popular fairy tales such as <i>Princess and the Frog</i>, <i>Sleeping Beauty</i> and <i>Rapunzel</i> into her narrative. Personally, I highly enjoy this aspect of the <i>Reckless</i> series, as it adds a clever twist and a deeper layer to the world. Just like her Inkworld, the Mirrorworld is a place that I love to explore and roam around in. It's a place where I feel at home. Jacob and Fox (Celeste) are incredibly close to my heart and, in my humble opinion, one of the best characters that Connie has ever written.<br /><br />I found the relationship drama (Jacob lowkey falling for Clara on their adventure) a bit tiresome, especially since I just wanted my two babies (Fox and Jacob) to strive, but I must admit that it added a bit of tension to the tale. Upon my reread, I was genuinely shocked by how sexual some of Connie's writing was. It's by no means explicit (mind you, she's not Sarah J. Mass ... thank God!) but I like the fact that the character's experiences matched their age, with Jacob already being 24 years old. It's kind of funny to see Connie write about young adults and not about teenagers.<br /><br />This time around I listened to the audiobook, narrated by Rainer Strecker, and I was surprised by its high production quality. The music at the end of each chapter fit the mood of the narrative so well and helped me to immerse myself in the story even more. The only gripe I had with the audiobook is the fact that Rainer Strecker chose to whisper the sentences that represented Jacob's inner thoughts, and that got hella annoying real fast. I HATE ASMR. ;)<br /><br />Overall, the series has managed to lure me in for a second time and I cannot wait to see what'll happen next. Will Jacob be able to save himself this time? What role will Fox play in their next adventure? Will the brothers be able to find their father who is probably lost somewhere behind the Mirror? What do the Dark Fairy and Kami'en plan next?</span>
  <a data-text-id="11771624591796358199" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

We were given little to no background information on the main characters, and then were thrown into a fantasy world where nothing was explained.   <span id="freeText2990599094800934504" style="display:none">I don't even know what to say about this book because I honestly don't have a clue what happened in it. It started off so random. We were given little to no background information on the main characters, and then were thrown into a fantasy world where nothing was explained. Funke has an amazing imagination, and I really enjoyed the Inkheart series, but this just didn't interest me. We're constantly reminded that Jacob and Will are brothers, but we never see any relationship between them, nor are we given any reason to care about their fate. I think this book could have been good, but it was poorly approached and I won't be reading the sequel. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4071596845123624824">This book was so confusing. I had to double check that it wasn't mistakenly marked as the first in a series as the reader is thrown into the story with absolutely no exposition or back story. When I did manage to get my footing this was a pretty basic fantasy tale with boring characters. The only ones I was rooting for were the jealous fox woman and the greedy dwarf.   <span id="freeText4071596845123624824" style="display:none">This book was so confusing. When I did manage to get my footing this was a pretty basic fantasy tale with boring characters. The only ones I was rooting for were the jealous fox woman and the greedy dwarf. This being a German book you could really see how it was influenced by the Grimms and there were some nice 'easter egg' references.<br /><br />Overall this is a series I will not be continuing with.</span>

<div id="review_167453336" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Andrés Velázquez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/691975-andr-s-vel-zquez"><img alt="Andrés Velázquez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1197929224p2/691975.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/167453336?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrés Velázquez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrés Velázquez" href="/user/show/691975-andr-s-vel-zquez">Andrés Velázquez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9788189776195" href="/book/show/10787380-reckless">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer167453336" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14699421837290494396">First when I read the first couple of chapters I felt a bit disapointed because I realized the style was meant like a fantasy adventure book for children. But as I keep reading the book became more and more engaging.<br/><br/>The dark twist in the fairy tale world may not be a new concept but is pretty well handled in this novel, sometimes when authors focus on writting this type of books they only develop certain aspects of the fantastic world delivering an uncreative, unimaginative book. On the contrary</span>
  <span id="freeText14699421837290494396" style="display:none">First when I read the first couple of chapters I felt a bit disapointed because I realized the style was meant like a fantasy adventure book for children. But as I keep reading the book became more and more engaging.<br /><br />The dark twist in the fairy tale world may not be a new concept but is pretty well handled in this novel, sometimes when authors focus on writting this type of books they only develop certain aspects of the fantastic world delivering an uncreative, unimaginative book. On the contrary, the world of Reckless is very immersive and is developed in a way that makes you feel that you are actually witnessing a vast world behind the mirror.<br /><br />Besides there´s not a dull moment in the book, making it a great light-page-turner read. There is one thing that can be criticized though, and that is that it lacks in the descriptive part, while character traits or simply the scenery or the mood could be described more thoroughly.<br /><br />All in all Funke created a pretty great dark fairy tale which I wouldn´t doubt on recommending.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14699421837290494396" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Something, however, stopped me from reading it previously.   <span id="freeText16608691148071890447" style="display:none">2.5 Stars<br /><br /><i> Read all my reviews on <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://urlphantomhive.booklikes.com">http://urlphantomhive.booklikes.com</a> </i><br /><br />The Petrified Flesh (or Reckless as it used to be called), is a series by Cornelia Funke that I have seen in the bookstore about a million times. Something, however, stopped me from reading it previously. I can't even begin to explain why, because her Inkworld trilogy is one of my favorite children's books and The Thief Lord I also enjoyed a lot. <br /><br />Maybe it was just a warning from myself, because now that I read it, it didn't feel right and I can't say that I enjoyed it. It felt part like a cheaper version of Inkworld, with another world behind the mirror, and also the characters didn't come to life for me (pun intended). It was not truly bad either, but just very forgettable. <br /><br />I was disappointed, and I haven't decided yet wether or not to continue with the series.</span>

<div id="review_286211543" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/286211543" />
    <a title="Stephanie Jobe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7984922-stephanie-jobe"><img alt="Stephanie Jobe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571890562p2/7984922.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/286211543?book_show_action=true">Feb 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephanie Jobe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephanie Jobe" href="/user/show/7984922-stephanie-jobe">Stephanie Jobe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9788189776195" href="/book/show/10787380-reckless">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer286211543" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13473488660993188531">I’ll start out with an interesting cover note, the one pictured here is the paperback copy that I have. Featured on the cover is Jacob as distinguished by the fact that his eyes are green, not blue or gold. Though the green swirlies made me unsure at first. The original cover the black with the frame and the green face, that is Will. Now a making fun of myself moment: notice those names? Jacob and Will… hmm that rings a bell… Jacob and Wilhelm… okay so yes they have the Grimm brothers name. The </span>
  <span id="freeText13473488660993188531" style="display:none">I’ll start out with an interesting cover note, the one pictured here is the paperback copy that I have. Featured on the cover is Jacob as distinguished by the fact that his eyes are green, not blue or gold. Though the green swirlies made me unsure at first. The original cover the black with the frame and the green face, that is Will. Now a making fun of myself moment: notice those names? Jacob and Will… hmm that rings a bell… Jacob and Wilhelm… okay so yes they have the Grimm brothers name. The shame is that is was over of a quarter of the way through a book filled with fairy tales made real before I realized the Reckless brothers were named after the Grimm brothers. Cue facepalm.<br /><br />So so far you know that we have a fairy tale land and two brothers. Their father disappeared when they were young. They’re mother recently died of cancer. For years older brother Jacob has been disappearing for huge chunks of time, but in some ways he never left their father’s study. In the room that they all avoid is a mirror that is a door into another world. A world that Jacob prefers over reality. Then Will stumbles in after him and is cursed and Jacob must find a way to save him.<br /><br />This is not a happy fairyland. The bad guys are worse and the happy endings aren’t necessarily true. Jacob’s best friend is Fox, a vixen who is actually a girl he once saved. Jacob Reckless has made a name for himself as a treasure hunter, finding legendary magic items. Then there is Will who trusts his brother absolutely even though he left so often. There are other interesting people to the cast but I don’t want to spoil anything. Jacob feels like a gallant hero, but you also see the vulnerable young man underneath.<br /><br />I started this not realizing there was going to be a second book but honestly I began to seriously suspect about halfway through. I’ve been avoiding series because they’re a reason for me to want to buy more books but well it’s Cornelia Funke, it’s fairly assured I’m going to buy what she puts out anyway. I love her characters and the worlds she creates. They always feel so complete to me. Complete immersion. I also love her writing, everything about it, and I suppose translator Oliver Latsch probably gets some credit for that, but I know I love everything she has written and not all of it was translated by him.<br /><br />This is definitely a book that could be read easily by a male or a female I think and it is a great crossover that is adult but would definitely be enjoyed by young adults as well. Sometimes I have issues writing when part of my gut is to just say: LOVE, LOVE, LOVE… READ IT!<br /><br />This is the first book of the Mirrorworld series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13473488660993188531" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_144989792" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/144989792" />
    <a title="Jackie &quot;the Librarian&quot;" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/289556-jackie-the-librarian"><img alt="Jackie &quot;the Librarian&quot;" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307387831p2/289556.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/144989792?book_show_action=true">Jan 31, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jackie &quot;the Librarian&quot;" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jackie &quot;the Librarian&quot;" href="/user/show/289556-jackie-the-librarian">Jackie &quot;the Librarian&quot;</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/289556-jackie-the-librarian?shelf=fairytalesretold">fairytalesretold</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/289556-jackie-the-librarian?shelf=youngadult">youngadult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/289556-jackie-the-librarian?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer144989792" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17133980062792391343">Retold fairy tales tend to be funny retellings with spunky heroines overcoming obstacles with help from magical animals, and meeting cute with their prince in disguise, or reformed thief. Not this time. This book isn't a BIT funny. <br/><br/>Jacob Reckless discovered the world on the other side of the mirror in his missing father's study years ago. It's a dangerous place that seems to be the origin of all our fairy tales, such as <i>Hansel and Gretel</i> (there are actual gingerbread houses with child-eating wit</span>
  <span id="freeText17133980062792391343" style="display:none">Retold fairy tales tend to be funny retellings with spunky heroines overcoming obstacles with help from magical animals, and meeting cute with their prince in disguise, or reformed thief. Not this time. This book isn't a BIT funny. <br /><br />Jacob Reckless discovered the world on the other side of the mirror in his missing father's study years ago. It's a dangerous place that seems to be the origin of all our fairy tales, such as <i>Hansel and Gretel</i> (there are actual gingerbread houses with child-eating witches in the forest) and <i>Sleeping Beauty</i>, although it looks like no prince ever made it through the wall of thorns to awaken her.<br /><br />Jacob survived all the dangers of his many explorations, but when his younger brother also finds his way through the mirror, he is not so lucky. Infected by a scratch from a Hentzen, Will is becoming one himself, slowly turning into a man made of living stone. It's up to Jacob to save him, if he can.<br /><br />By the author of <i>Inkheart</i>, this is a very dark fantasy world, and while I was engaged by the story, it wasn't a particularly FUN read, but instead a tense one. I liked that it was a fantasy with male protagonists, as there are so many for girls, and not so many for boys. I liked that it was serious, not a spoof, that the witches were real, and would eat you if given a chance, and that the fairies were amoral and beautiful and scary. I liked the very real sense of how much was at stake. I didn't mind that it seemed to be the first book of a series, as the story comes to a good ending point with enough resolution to be satisfying in itself.<br /><br />I liked the references to fairy tales, but was confused by the Hentzen, the stone men. Are they a German fairy tale thing, perhaps? <br />Recommended for ages 11 and up.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17133980062792391343" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9780307583260" href="/book/show/7571140-reckless">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1070527967" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9572253605542461802">Back when I read Ms. Funke's Inkheart series, and liked it. I found later that it was a mixed bag as to who liked those and who didn't. The same seems to be true here. <br/><br/>This is the first in the Mirror World series. The series is called that because...you get to the world by passing through a mirror.<br/><br/>Who'd a thought it?<br/><br/>See our young protagonist's father disappeared through the looking-glass when our said protagonist was a boy (much like the protagonist of Inkheart's mother fell through a book I sup</span>
  <span id="freeText9572253605542461802" style="display:none">Back when I read Ms. Funke's Inkheart series, and liked it. I found later that it was a mixed bag as to who liked those and who didn't. The same seems to be true here. <br /><br />This is the first in the Mirror World series. The series is called that because...you get to the world by passing through a mirror.<br /><br />Who'd a thought it?<br /><br />See our young protagonist's father disappeared through the looking-glass when our said protagonist was a boy (much like the protagonist of Inkheart's mother fell through a book I suppose) so our hero after finding his way through said mirror into said mirror world just keeps doing so, more and more. He establishes a life in that world where Fairy Tale "stuff" works and exists... He's searching for his father.<br /><br />Unfortunately his younger brother follows him through, is not really cut out for a magic realm and "bad stuff" ensues.<br /><br />So, as I said, I liked the book. It's one of those odd books that seems a bit young yet deals with more mature subject matter and story but it works. I would give my standard heads up that parents or guardians might want to read this before their younger charges.<br /><br />Recommended, enjoy.<br /> <br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4518789179537654331">Cornelia Strikes Again!<br/><br/>I have to say that Cornelia Funke is one of my all-time favorite authors. She is fantastic at creating an entire new world with inspiring 3-dimensional characters. Believable characters. This is just more proof of her wonderful story-telling.<br/>Jacob Reckless is a character we can all understand, even if we don't want to. What happens to a child neglected? One who's father is gone?   <span id="freeText4518789179537654331" style="display:none">Cornelia Strikes Again!<br /><br />I have to say that Cornelia Funke is one of my all-time favorite authors. She is fantastic at creating an entire new world with inspiring 3-dimensional characters. Believable characters. This is just more proof of her wonderful story-telling.<br />Jacob Reckless is a character we can all understand, even if we don't want to. What happens to a child neglected? One who's father is gone? Slipping farther and farther away from the family he still has until he finally pulls his brother into the frightening and dangerous world of the Mirror? <br />This book is full of characters new and old, if you only stop and look. It is a world of dark fairy tales and thrills, along with a little romance. Adventures that can end up hurting (or killing) you! <br />Reckless is a short book filled to the brim with good writing. Me personally? I can't wait for the next installment of Cornelia Funke's latest masterpiece! </span>

<div id="review_123094387" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/123094387" />
    <a title="Kogiopsis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1462364-kogiopsis"><img alt="Kogiopsis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494267218p2/1462364.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/123094387?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kogiopsis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kogiopsis" href="/user/show/1462364-kogiopsis">Kogiopsis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer123094387" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3689871172602799556">Ahh, Cornelia Funke. I was in middle school when <i>Inkheart</i> first appeared in the American market and quickly took my age group by storm. <i>Inkspell</i> followed, and I picked up <i>The Thief Lord</i> too - it was a great audiobook. But… somehow I never read <i>Inkdeath</i>, and Funke slipped off of my author radar - until Megan told me <i>Reckless</i> was one of her favorite series.<br/><br/>I don’t know it it’ll become one of mine, but it certainly was an interesting experience. At first, I thought it was a middle-grade book, becau</span>
  <span id="freeText3689871172602799556" style="display:none">Ahh, Cornelia Funke. I was in middle school when <i>Inkheart</i> first appeared in the American market and quickly took my age group by storm. <i>Inkspell</i> followed, and I picked up <i>The Thief Lord</i> too - it was a great audiobook. But… somehow I never read <i>Inkdeath</i>, and Funke slipped off of my author radar - until Megan told me <i>Reckless</i> was one of her favorite series.<br /><br />I don’t know it it’ll become one of mine, but it certainly was an interesting experience. At first, I thought it was a middle-grade book, because the syntax and word choice feels a little young to me; however, it quickly became apparent that this book is far from middle-grade, and the syntax is probably more a result of translation than anything else. Indeed, <i>Reckless</i> is a dark and mature take on fairy tales - rather to be expected from a German author, given that Germany is the birthplace of many such stories in their grimmest variations. (Heh.)<br /><br />In broad strokes, the Mirrorworld reminded me of similar concepts - Mercedes Lackey’s 500 Kingdoms, for example, is another ‘all fairy tales exist in one place’ setting. However, the Mirrorworld feels more dynamic than many other variations on the same theme. I was particularly struck by the inclusion of technological development, and the jarring pace at which it has changed the world; it evokes the Industrial Revolution of our world. The utility of fairy tale objects (like a Rapunzel hair capable of holding any weight and growing to any length needed) was also a great aspect. This is the kind of secondary world that you feel strongly has economics just as complicated as ours, even if you don’t see them in detail.<br /><br />The characters, unfortunately, were difficult for me to connect to. Again, this may partly be due to translation, but particularly at the beginning of the book I just… didn’t particularly care, especially about Will and Jacob’s sibling relationship. At the beginning of the book, their bond has already been strained for years; we don’t really see what holds them together, just what pulls them apart. Between that and the fact that Will eventually loses his ability to think for himself, and I really only got a sense of <i>obligation</i> from Jacob to his brother, not affection or love. I also found myself confused when it came to character ages, particularly in the case of Fox - at first I thought she was significantly younger than Jacob, but she seems to be framed for a future romance with him, so I must have been wrong in my initial estimate that she was around 14.<br /><br />I do plan on reading at least the second book, and probably the third as well - hopefully the problems of adjustment and connection I had with the characters will be ameliorated now that I’m already familiar with them to a degree. Additionally, I <i>really</i> loved the sting at the end - magic with a heavy cost is one of my favorite worldbuilding concepts, and the high price of victory in this first installment promises interesting recovery in the sequels.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3689871172602799556" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2164774709" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2164774709" />
    <a title="Christian Martinez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/72670531-christian-martinez"><img alt="Christian Martinez" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2164774709?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christian Martinez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christian Martinez" href="/user/show/72670531-christian-martinez">Christian Martinez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2164774709" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14937694507715030891">Reckless is a great book; though, she should have put more information between the relationships of Jacob and his friends on a personal level. I enjoyed this book immensely and I would love to give this book five stars, but i would have to give it four stars. Though the book contains mystery, drama, and action, it is missing an important aspect that makes the reader want to keep reading to see what would happen next. Romance! Romance between Jacob and Fox is hinted throughout the entirety of the</span>
  <span id="freeText14937694507715030891" style="display:none">Reckless is a great book; though, she should have put more information between the relationships of Jacob and his friends on a personal level. I enjoyed this book immensely and I would love to give this book five stars, but i would have to give it four stars. Though the book contains mystery, drama, and action, it is missing an important aspect that makes the reader want to keep reading to see what would happen next. Romance! Romance between Jacob and Fox is hinted throughout the entirety of the novel and Cornelia, not giving enough signs to make it clear to any reader that they like each other, is not making the case any better. I am not hating or throwing shade at Cornelia for this, but all I’m saying is that the next book better have some serious romance between Jacob and Fox. Anyways, moving on, I really enjoyed this book and I absolutely love the tension throughout the book. This books drags you in and leaves you with a cliffhanger. I absolutely hate but love how it ended because it just leaves you with the questions “What will happen to Jacob in the mirror world?” “Will he survive and find a cure?” and so many more! I would read it over and over again, but there are so many more books in the world to be read. Though there are minor things that I would change in the book, I would recommend this book for anyone who wants to sit down and enjoy an adventure!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14937694507715030891" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
